Whitney anukramaс╣З─л

[Brahman.тАФс╣Ыcas triс╣Е┼Ыat.1 ─Бdityadevaty─Бs. 1. jagat─л; 1-8. try-avas─Бna;4 1-4 тМКintending 2-5?тМЛ. atijagat─л;2 6, 7, 19. atyaс╣гс╣нi;3 8, 11, 16. atidhс╣Ыti; 9. 5-p. ┼Ыakvar─л; 10-23, 16, 18-19, 24. try-avas─Бna;4 10. 8-p. dhс╣Ыti; 12. kс╣Ыti; 13. prakс╣Ыti; 14-15. 5-p. ┼Ыakvar─л; 17. 5-p. vir─Бс╕Н ati┼Ыakvar─л; 18. bhurig aс╣гс╣нi; 24. vir─Бс╕Н atyaс╣гс╣нi; 1-8 тМКintending 1-5?тМЛ. 6-p.; тМК6-8,тМЛ 11-13, 16, 18-19, 24. 7-p.5 20. kakubh; 21. 4-p. upariс╣гс╣н─Бdbс╣Ыhat─л; 22. anuс╣гс╣нubh; 23. nicс╣Ыd bс╣Ыhat─л (22-23. yajuс╣г─л dve;6 2-p); 25, 26. anuс╣гс╣нubh; 27, 30. jagat─л; 28, 29. triс╣гс╣нubh.]

Whitney

Comment

The Anukr. has some bad readings and confusions in its account of the book, but they do not concern things of much consequence. тМКSo Whitney, in a note to vs. 5, which note I have transposed hither. He had altered (as often, for brevity) the order of his excerpts from the Anukr.: but I have restored them in this case to the order of the original. Moreover, there are several trifling items which he has omitted or misapprehended: and these I have added or tried to set right without marking them with the usual ell-brackets.тМЛ

тМКNotes to the Anukramaс╣З─л-excerpts. 1тМКThe text begins, viс╣г─Бsahir с╣Ыcas triс╣Е┼Ыat, which is taken from the Old Anukr.: see p. 812.тМЛ 2тМКAs to the structure and count of vss. 1-5, see page 805, ┬╢ 4тМЛ 3тМКText reads simply udih─лti dve asati sad atyaс╣гс╣нayaс╕е: read ity aс╣гс╣нayaс╕е? or, perhaps, ity atyaс╣гс╣нayaс╕е? but see note to verse 7.тМЛ 4тМКThe statements concerning the try-avas─Бna verses are given in two instalments and are entirely correct, although the Berlin edition makes them seem partially incorrect: vss. 1-5 are 3-av. in both ed’s; 6-8 and 10-13, 16, 18-19, 24 are 3-av. in the mss. and the Bombay ed. and are 4-av. in the Berlin ed.: see page 805, ┬╢ 5, above.тМЛ 5тМКThe text says aс╣гс╣н─Бu [should be pa├▒ca] с╣гaс╣нpad─Бс╕е, ┼Ыeс╣г─Бс╕е saptapad─Бс╕е: ’the rest’ (┼Ыeс╣г─Бс╕е) are those that remain after taking out from the verses thus far discussed those verses (1-8[5], 9-10, 14-15, 17) the number of whose p─Бdas has been already stated: and the Anukr. therefore means (after emending aс╣гс╣н─Бu to pa├▒ca), ‘verses 1-5 are of 6 p─Бdas, while the rest,тАФnamely verses [6-8,] 11-13, 16, 18-19, 24,тАФare of 7 p─Бdas’; and this is quite correctтМЛ 6тМКSee note to vs. 22 and cf. note to xvi. 8. 1.тМЛ

тМКPartly proseтАФverses 20-23: see ┬╢ 1, on this page.тМЛ

The hymn, or anuv─Бka, or book, occurs (except vss. 13, 14, 24) also in P─Бipp. xviii., following immediately upon what represents our xvi.

Griffith

A prayer to Indra, Identified with Vishnu and the Sun, for the love of Gods, men, and beasts, general protection and prosperity, and all earthly and heavenly blessings

Whitney
Translation
  1. Indra of mighty power, overpowering, having overpowered, very
    powerful, overpowering, power-winning (saho-j├нt), heaven-winning,
    kine-winning, booty-winning, to be praised (─лс╕Н), by name, do I call:
    may I be long-lived.
Notes
Griffith

Vanquishing, overpowering, a conqueror, exceeding strong, Victorious, winner of the light, winner of cattle and of spoil,. Indra by name, adorable, I call: a long, long life be mine!

Whitney
Translation
  1. Arise, arise, O sun; arise upon me with splendor; both let my hater
    be subject to me, and let not me be subject to my hater.тАФThine, O
    Vishс╣Зu, are heroisms manifold; do thou fill us with cattle of all forms;
    set me in comfort in the highest firmament (vy├▓man).
Notes

Ppp. reads in the concluding p─Бda of the refrain svadh─Бy─Бс╣Б no dh-; the
comm. also has svadh─Бy─Бm. The mss. commit the absurdity throughout of
setting no avas─Бna between the verse proper and the refrain; we have,
as required by the sense, introduced it in our text; тМКthe matter is
further discussed above, p. 805, ┬╢ 5тМЛ. The refrain is, as usual,
represented in vss. 7-18 only by the word t├бva in the mss. (except in
R., which fills it out a little further). тМКWith reference to the main
stock of the verse, the comm. cites most appositely TB. iii. 7. 6┬▓┬│, ├║d
ag─Бd ay├бm ─Бdity├│ vi┼Ыvena s├бhas─Б sah├б: dviс╣г├бntam m├бma randh├бyan m├│ ah├бс╣Б
dviс╣гat├│ radham, although it does not appear why he did not cite rather
our verse 24 a-d, below, which see.тМЛ тМКThe refrain seems to count as
11: 12 + 11 = 34 syllables with the Anukr.; but the true triс╣гс╣нubh
cadences (vi┼Ыv├бr┼лp─Бiс╕е, v├нoman) of its second and third p─Бdas suggest
the suspicion of metrical disorder in the prior part of each of those
p─Бdas. One is tempted to think of pс╣Ыс╣З─лhi as an ill-considered
modernization of p┼лrdhi; and to wish that m─Б (before dhehi) might
be excised, as superfluous in meter and in sense and as making a harsh
change from plural (nas) to singular.тАФThe change from singular to
plural as between the main stock and the refrain, considering the
looseness of their connection, is not to be called harsh.тМЛ

Griffith

Rise up, O Surya, rise thou up; with strength and splendour rise on me. Let him who hates me be my thrall; let me not be a thrall to him. Manifold are thy great deeds, thine, O Vishnu. Sate us with cattle of all forms and colours: set me in happiness, in loftiest heaven.

Translation
  1. Arise, arise, O sun; arise upon me with splendor; both those whom I
    see and those whom I do notтАФamong them make thou favor for me. Thine, O
    Vishс╣Зu etc. etc.

Griffith

Rise up, O Surya, rise thou up; with strength and splendour rise on me. Make me the favourite of all, of those I see and do not see. Manifold are thy great deeds, thine, O Vishnu.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Let them not damage thee in the sea, within the watersтАФthey who
    approach there having fetters; quitting imprecation, thou hast ascended
    that sky; be thou then gracious to us; may we be in thy favor.тАФThine, O
    Vishс╣Зu etc. etc.
Notes

Ppp. reads in b p─Б┼Ыinam, and in c ─Б ruha et─Бn. The verse
counts most naturally 78 syllables (11 ├Ч 4: 34); a proper atidhс╣Ыti has
76. Bp. reads in d ─Б╠Б; rukс╣гaс╕е; D.Kp. and all SPP’s authorities have ─Б╠Б;
ar-, which is doubtless the true pada-text.

Griffith

Let not the fowlers who are standing ready injure thee in the flood, within the waters. Ascend this heaven, leaving each curse behind thee, Favour us: let thy gracious love attend us. Manifold are thy great deeds, thine, O Vishnu.

Translation
  1. Do thou, O Indra, with propitious aids, be most wealful to
    usтАФascending to the triple heaven of the heaven (d├нv), besung unto
    soma-drinking, having a dear abode (-dh─Б╠Бman) unto well-being.тАФThine, O
    Vishnu etc. etc.
Notes

Ppp. reads in a indro adbhi┼Ы (┼Ы-). The comm. gives us our choice
between -sth─Бna and -tejas as meanings of -dh─Бman in e. The
verse has two syllables too many for a regular dhс╣Ыti (72); тМКit reads
properly as 5 ├Ч 8 and 34; but p─Бda a may be read as 6тМЛ.

Griffith

Be thou most gracious unto us, Indra, with favourable aid, Rising to heaven’s third sphere, invoked with song to quaff the Soma juice, loving thy home to make us blest. Manifold are thy great deeds, thine, O Vishnu.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Thou, O Indra, art all-conquering, all-gaining (sarva-v├нd); much
    invoked [art] thou, O Indra; do thou, O Indra, send onward this
    well-invoking praise; be thou gracious to us; may we be in thy
    favor.тАФThine, O Vishс╣Зu etc. etc.
Notes

Ppp. reads in a vi┼Ыvavit; and instead of our d (= 8 d) it
has ┼Ыiv─Бbhis tanubhir abhi nas sajasva. The verse is a true atidhс╣Ыti
by number of syllables, but very irregular in structure (8 + 10: 13 +
11: 34 = 76).

Griffith

Thou art the vanquisher of all, O Indra, omniscient Indra, and invoked of many. Indra, send forth this hymn that fitly lauds thee. Favour us let thy gracious love attend us. Manifold are thy great deeds, thine, O Vishnu.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Unharmed in the heaven (d├нv), also on earth, art thou; they have
    not attained thy greatness in the atmosphere; increasing with unharmed
    worship (br├бhman), do thou there, O Indra, being in the heaven
    (d├нv), bestow protection (┼Ы├бrman) on us.тАФThine, O Vishс╣Зu etc. etc.
Notes

Ppp. reads divaс╣г p- in a. тМКin d, all of SPP’s authorities give
с╣г├бс╣Е or s├бn: and W’s Collation Book notes nothing to the contrary;
butтМЛ the comm. omits the word, as the meter plainly requires. The verse
(11 + 12: 11 + 12: 34 = 80) is by number of syllables an exact kс╣Ыti.

Griffith

In heaven and on the earth thou art uninjured, none reach thy greatness in the air’s mid region. Increasing by inviolate devotion as such in heaven grant us pro- tection, Indra. Manifold are thy great deeds, thine, O Vishnu.

Translation
  1. What body of thine, O Indra, is in the waters, what on the earth,
    what within the fire; what of thine, O Indra, is in the heaven-gaining

    thou protection upon us.тАФThine, O Vishс╣Зu etc. etc.
Notes

In nearly all our mss. (all save D. and R.p.m.) vy─Бpitha (p.
viре░─Бpitha) is most strangely left unaccented, and the reading was in
our text emended to vy─Б╠Бpitha, in accordance with the invariable
accentuation of such forms in RV. and AV. elsewhere. But a minority of
SPP’s authorities are reported by him as accenting vy─Бpith├б, and he
accordingly prints vy─Бpith├б in his edition (our D.R.p.m. have the
same). The ‘purifying one’ is doubtless here the wind (v─Бyu: so
comm.). The verse (12 + 16: 12 + 12: 34 = 86) counts two more syllables
than a proper prakс╣Ыti.

Griffith

Grant us protection, Indra, with that body of thine that is on earth, in fire, in waters, That dwells within light-finding Pavamana, wherewith thou hast pervaded air’s mid region. Manifold are thy great deeds, thine, O Vishnu.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Thou goest about Tс╣Ыita (?), thou about the fountain of a thousand
    streams, the heaven-gaining council.тАФThine, O Vishс╣Зu etc. etc.
Notes

All the mss., and hence both editions, read tс╣Ыt├бm in a; but the
ms. of the comm. has tritam, and we cannot well believe that the
latter is not the true reading; though the sense of the whole verse is
extremely obscure. The comm. explains tritam mysteriously, as either
vist─лrс╣Зam antarikс╣гam or megh─Бir ─Бvс╣Ыtam udakam. Vidatha, he says, =
yaj├▒a. The verse is capable of being read as 56 syllables. Ppp. puts
it after our verse 17.

Griffith

Round Trita, round the spring with thousand currents thou goest, round the light-finding assembly. Manifold are thy great deeds, thine, O Vishnu.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Thou defendest the four directions; thou shinest abroad with
    brightness (┼Ыocis) unto the two firmaments (n├бbhas); thou pursuest
    (anusth─Б) all these beings; thou, knowing, followest (anu-i) the way
    of righteousness.тАФThine, O Vishс╣Зu etc. etc.
Notes

The saс╣Бhit─Б-mss. read vidv─Б╠Бс╣Еs t├бv├й тАЩd between verse and refrain. The
whole (11 + 11: 12 + 11: 34 = 79) reads naturally as three more
syllables than belong to an atidhс╣Ыti.

Griffith

Thou guardest well the four celestial regions, pervading heaven, and earth with light and splendour. Thou givest help to all these living creatures, and, knowing,. followest the path of Order. Manifold are thy great deed, thine, O Vishnu.

Whitney
Translation
  1. With five thou heatest upward (p├бr─Бn╠Д), with one hitherward; thou
    goest driving off the imprecation in good weather (sud├нna).тАФThine, O
    Vishс╣Зu etc. etc.
Notes

The comm. supplies, as is natural, d─лdhiti or mar─лci ‘ray’ for the
missing noun, and explains the five as required in order to illuminate
so many worlds beyond the sun. But Ppp. reads instead saptabhiс╣г p-
‘with seven.’ тМКWith reference to the rays, Griffith (note to xi. 1. 36)
cites Mah─лdhara as quoted by Eggeling on ┼ЫB. i. 9. 3┬╣тБ╢.тМЛ The comm. has
the bad reading n─Бdham─Бnas for b─Бdh-. We have to resolve a saс╣Бdhi
in a in order to make 58 syllables in the verse.

Griffith

With five thou sendest heat: with one removing the curse thou comest in bright sunshine hither. Manifold are thy great deeds, thine, O Vishnu.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Thou art Indra, thou great Indra, thou the world, thou Praj─Бpati;
    for thee the sacrifice is extended; to thee the offerers make
    oblation.тАФThine, O Vishс╣Зu etc. etc.
Notes

Ppp. reads viс╣гс╣Зus for lokas in b, and, in c yaj─Бyate for
vi t─Бyate. Our Bp.P.M.W. T.R.p.m. also have j─Бyate for t─Бyate. To
make the verse only bhurig aс╣гс╣нi (65 syll.), we have to read the first
p─Бda as seven syllables, though it easily makes eight. In V─Бit. 3. 3 the
verse, with vi. 5. 2, is made to accompany a s─Бс╣Бn─Бyya offering to
Indra, in the dar┼Ыap┼лrс╣Зam─Бsa ceremony. In our edition, the с╣Б of
tv├бс╣Б before lok├бs is lost in printing.

Griffith

Indra art thou, Mahendra thou, thou art the world, the Lord of Life. To thee is sacrifice performed: worshippers offer gifts to thee. Manifold are thy great deeds, thine, O Vishnu.

Whitney
Translation
  1. In the non-existent is the existent made firm; in the existent is
    being (bh┼лt├б) made firm; being is set in what is to be; what is to be
    is made firm in being. Thine, O Vishс╣Зu etc. etc.
Notes

Ppp. combines bhavy─Б тАЭhitam тМКdouble sandhi after -e as at ix. 1. 14тМЛ
in c, and has sam─Бhitam for pratiс╣гс╣нhitam in d. The verse,
like 6 and 7, lacks two syllables of a full atyaс╣гс╣нi; тМКbut see note to
vs. 7 and p. 806, ┬╢ 6, note 3, aboveтМЛ.

Griffith

What is based on what is not: the present lies on that which is.. Present on future is imposed and future on the present based. Manifold are thy great deeds, thine, O Vishnu. Sate us with cattle of all varied colour. Set me in happiness, in loftiest heaven.

Translation
  1. Brilliant (┼Ыukr├б) art thou; shiny art thou; as thou art shiny by
    the shining one (bhr─Б╠Бjant), so may I by the shining one shine.
Notes

The Ppp. text of this verse is in confusion. Our P.M.I.T. combine
(second time) bhr─Бj├▓ тАШsi, as if we had here, as the first time, asi
(instead of ├бsi). The first p─Бda is the same with the beginning of ii.
11. 5. MS. iv. 9. 5 has passages resembling this verse and the next.
This prose bit is a queer kakubh: тМКthe kakubh calls for 8 + 12 + 8 =
28; and this may be read as 8 + 11 + 9тМЛ.

Griffith

Bright art thou, and refulgent: as thou shinest with splendour so I fain would shine with splendour.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Brightness art thou, bright art thou; as thou by brightness art
    bright, so may I by both cattle and Brahman-splendor be bright (ruc).
Notes

Our P.M.T. have again (second time) roc├▓ тАШsi; тМКand one of SPP’s
pada-mss. has correspondingly asi without accentтМЛ. The MS. version
is in some respects better: ruc├нr asi ruc├▓ (or rocy├▓) тАШsi s├б y├бth─Б
tv├бс╣Б rucy─Б╠Б r├│casa ev├бm ah├бс╣Б rucy─Б╠Б rociс╣г─лya. Ppp. also gives rociс╣г─лya.
тМКFor ruciс╣г─лya or roc-, see Gram. ┬з 907.тМЛ The metrical definition
of the Anukr. is absurd, the “verse” being prose, and having only three
possible divisions; it can be made 36 syllables by reading roco asi
either in a or in b. It is used in V─Бit. 14. 2, in the
agniс╣гс╣нoma ceremony.

Griffith

Lustre art thou, illuming: as thou glowest with lustre so I too would shine with cattle, with all the lustre of a Brahman’s station.

Griffith

With all his fiery fervour this Aditya hath gone up on high, Giving my foes into my hand. Let me not by my foeman’s prey. Manifold are thy great deeds, thine, O Vishnu. Sate us with cattle of all varied colours. Set me in happiness, in loftiest heaven.

Whitney
Translation
  1. O ─Аditya, thou hast ascended a boat of a hundred oars in order to
    well-being; thou hast made me to pass over the day, make thou me
    likewise (satr─Б╠Б) to pass over the night.
Notes

The comm. explains satr─Б╠Б by sah─Бi тАЩva, ahn─Б saha; he gives also as
admissible alternative explanation “I have ascended thee as a boat”
etc., understanding the second person to be used as a first! Ppp. reads,
in fact, ─Б тАЩruham; and, in c, ahar с╣Зo тАШty.

Griffith

Thou for our weal, Aditya, hast mounted thy ship with hundred oars. Thou hast transported me to day: so bear me evermore to night.

Whitney
Translation
  1. O sun, thou hast ascended a boat of a hundred oars in order to
    well-being; thou hast made me to pass over the night, make thou me
    likewise to pass over the day.
Notes

Passages analogous and in part accordant with the two preceding verses
are found in MB. ii. 5. 13, 14. Ppp. reads in a ─Б тАЩrikс╣гam; and, in
c, r─Бtr─л с╣Зo тАШty.

Griffith

Thou for our weal, O Surya, hast mounted thy ship with hundred oars. Thou hast transported me to night: so bear me evermore to day.

Translation
  1. With Praj─Бpati’s worship (br├бhman) [as] defense am I covered,
    with Ka┼Ыyapa’s light and splendor; long-lived, of finished heroism,
    vigorous (? v├нh─Бyas), having a thousand life-times, well-made, may I
    go about.

Griffith

Encompassed by Prajapati’s devotion as shield, with Kasyapa’s bright light and splendour, Reaching old age, may I made strong and mighty live through a thousand years with happy fortune.

Translation
  1. Encompassed with worship [as] defense am I, with Ka┼Ыyapa’s light
    and splendor; let not the arrows that are the gods’ attain me, nor those
    of men, let loose in order to slay (vadhy─Б╠Бya).
Notes

SPP. reports his pada-mss. as reading y─Б╠Б instead of y─Б╠Бс╕е at end of
c; I have not observed the blunder in ours. All, both his and ours,
give ├бvaре░sс╣Ыс╣гс╣н─Б instead of -с╣н─Бс╕е in d. The comm. adds the
visarga in both words. A part of the verse is wanting in Ppp.

Griffith

Compassed am I with prayer, my shield and armour; compassed with Kasyapa’s bright light and splendour. Let not shafts reach me shot from heaven against me, nor those sent forth by men for my destruction.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Guarded by righteousness and by all the seasons, guarded by what is
    and by what is to be am I; let not evil attain me, nor death; I
    interpose with a sea of speech.
Notes

That is, I set my uttered charms like a sea between me and them.

Griffith

Guarded am I by Order and the Seasons, protected by the past and by the future. Let not distress, yea, let not Death come nigh me: with water of my speech have I o’erwhelmed them.

рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдгреА: реирептИТ(рдЛрддреЗрди) рд╕рддреНрдпрдзрд░реНрдореЗрдг (рдЧреБрдкреНрддрдГ) рд░рдХреНрд╖рд┐рддрдГ (рдЛрддреБрднрд┐рдГ) рд╡рд╕рдиреНрддрд╛рджрд┐рдХрд╛рд▓реИрдГ (рдЪ) (рд╕рд░реНрд╡реИрдГ) (рднреВрддреЗрди) рдЕрддреАрддреЗрди (рдЧреБрдкреНрддрдГ) (рднрд╡реНрдпреЗрди) рднрд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдпрддрд╛ (рдЪ) (рдЕрд╣рдореН) рдЙрдкрд╛рд╕рдХрдГ (рдорд╛) рдорд╛рдореН (рдорд╛рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрддреН) рдорд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрдпрд╛рддреН (рдкрд╛рдкреНрдорд╛) рдкрд╛рдкрдореН (рдорд╛) рдирд┐рд╖реЗрдзреЗ (рдЙрдд) рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ (рдореГрддреНрдпреБрдГ) рдорд░рдгрдореН (рдЕрдиреНрддрд░реНрджрдзреЗ) рдЕрдиреНрддрд░реНрдзрд╛рдирдВ рдХрд░реЛрдорд┐ (рдЕрд╣рдореН) (рд╕рд▓рд┐рд▓реЗрди) рдЬрд▓реЗрди (рд╡рд╛рдЪрдГ) рд╡реЗрджрд╡рд╛рдгреНрдпрд╛рдГ рее

Whitney
Translation
  1. Let Agni [as] guardian protect me all about; let the sun, rising,
    thrust [away] the fetters of death; out-shining dawns, firm
    mountainsтАФlet a thousand breaths abide (─Б-yat) in me.
Notes

Ppp. reads in a gopaс╣г pari, transposes p─Бdas b and c
(corrupting to vicchant─лr, and combining uс╣гasaс╣г p-), and ends d
with mayu te ramant─Бm; and it then adds our xviii. 4. 49. The
connection of our c is obscure; the comm. understands mс╣Ыtyup─Б┼Ы─Бn
nudant─Бm or else m─Бm anugс╣Ыhс╣Зantu: the former is possible. тМКThe verse
is to be read as 12 + 11: 12 + 11.тМЛ

тМКHere ends the first and sole anuv─Бka, with 1 hymn and 30 verses. The
words prathamo тАШnuv─Бkaс╕е are not printed here in either edition, but
are found in several of W’s mss. The quotation from the Old Anukr. is
ity etat samanukr─Бntam с╣Ыcas triс╣Е┼Ыad “viс╣г─Бsahiс╕е."тМЛ

тМКHere ends also the thirty-second prap─Бс╣нhaka.тМЛ

Griffith

On every side let Agni guard and keep me; the rising Sun drive off the snares of Mrityu! Let brightly flushing Mornings, firm-set mountains, and lives a thousand be with me united.

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рдкрд╛рджрдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреА

рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдгреА: рейрежтИТ(рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ) рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдордпрдГ рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рдГ (рдорд╛) рдорд╛рдореН (рдЧреЛрдкреНрддрд╛) рд░рдХреНрд╖рдХрдГ (рдкрд░рд┐рдкрд╛рддреБ) рдкрд░рд┐рддреЛ рд░рдХреНрд╖рддреБ (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рддрдГ) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддрдГ (рдЙрджреНрдпрдиреН) рдЙрджрдпрдВ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреН (рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдГ)рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдкреНрд░реЗрд░рдХрдГ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ (рдиреБрджрддрд╛рдореН) рдЕрдкрд╕рд╛рд░рдпрддреБ (рдореГрддреНрдпреБрдкрд╛рд╢рд╛рдиреН) рдорд░рдгрдмрдиреНрдзрд╛рдиреН (рд╡реНрдпреБрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддреАрдГ) рд╡реНрдпреБрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддреНрдпрд╛рдГред рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рдГ (рдкрд░реНрд╡рддрд╛рдГ) рд╢реИрд▓рд╛рдГ (рдзреНрд░реБрд╡рд╛рдГ)рджреГрдврд╛рдГ (рд╕рд╣рд╕реНрд░рдореН) рд╕рд╣рд╕реНрд░рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░реЗрдг (рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдГ) рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рд╕рдкреНрд░рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рд╕рд╛рдГредрд╢рд╛рд░реАрд░рд┐рдХрд╛рддреНрдорд┐рдХрдкрд░рд╛рдХреНрд░рдорд╛рдГ (рдордпрд┐) рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рдирд┐ (рдЖ) рд╕рдордиреНрддрд╛рддреН (рдпрддрдиреНрддрд╛рдореН) рдпрддреНрдирд╢реАрд▓рд╛рднрд╡рдиреНрддреБ рее
